Life and Living (3) 264

— Li Ying

[Okay?] I’ll go back, can you let me wander around a little bit more? His wife was so gentle, her smile, her words, left A-Lao with no choice. He looked again at her five-month-pregnant belly, and walked back towards the riverbank, saying as he went:

[You must go back before I come back with more mud.] He said, walking and turning his head back repeatedly.

After dinner, it was already dark. A-Lao heard his wife say that her stomach hurt a little. He was stunned for a moment, and suddenly a wave of darkness washed over him. But, he brushed it off with a cold glance and said to his wife:

[You go to bed, I’ll wash the dishes.]

So his wife went to bed, and A-Lao did all the things his wife was supposed to do. His heart was so flustered, he didn't know what to do. Then, he lit the lamp and ran to his wife's bedside.

His wife's stomach, she said, was hurting more and more. At first, she could still talk to him and answer his questions, but later she started rolling around in bed, just moaning [It hurts!][It hurts!]

A-Lao really didn't know what to do. He wanted to say: [I told you to come back earlier, you didn't listen, look what's happened….] But he couldn't say it, it would only make his wife feel worse. And it wasn't her fault either, he should blame himself. If he had money to hire someone, none of this would have happened!

He was afraid something bad would happen. He prayed, to get a doctor, but not only did he not have money, but there were none to be found in the countryside!

He kept praying, that was all he could do.

His wife writhed in pain, rolling, crying, screaming, how unbearable. He almost cried! His wife didn't say a word of blame to him, which made him feel even worse. He thought that at least his wife should say: [You poor wretch!]

After a long time, his wife seemed a little better, and A-Lao felt a little relieved. He thought that maybe nothing bad would happen. He prayed, praying for God's blessing.

But heaven does not care about these things. After a while, his wife's stomach started hurting even more severely. A-Rong panicked.

Everything is not something that heaven or God can protect, but rather something that follows the conditions of nature. For example: A-Rong had no money, so his wife had to work in the fields with a big belly, getting tired. The creature inside her changed, and in the end, after several bouts of severe pain, she finally miscarried, and the bed was stained with blood. Looking at the unrecognizable lump of flesh, A-Rong's wife, who had not yet lost her life, finally said several angry words to her husband, who was carefully attending to her:

[Can't we have a child? Poverty, poor people are really not human. But why are we poor? Aren't we working from morning till night? Why can those who are idle and do nothing have money and have children and grandchildren, while we who work so hard are so poor that we can't even have children? Tell me, are poor people really not human?….]

A-Rong just listened quietly, holding his wife's hand tightly, two lines of tears hanging in his eyes. After a while, he said angrily:

[No matter what! Poor people are also people, they also want to live, they must have children. We'll have more! One day, we will turn things around!]

His wife nodded weakly, and then used her weak hands to hug A-Lao tightly, saying intermittently: [Success… Want to have… a child! Poor people are… also… a life! Must have… a child…] On their two aching hearts, there seemed to flicker a glimmer of light. (The End)

George Bernard Shaw Visits China 265

— Xuan

The veteran of the British literary scene, George Bernard Shaw, is currently on a world tour and will soon arrive in Shanghai.

The Chinese intelligentsia probably haven't forgotten that this old Mr. Shaw was enthusiastically introduced during the May Fourth Movement ten years ago, right? Mentioning Ibsen will likely bring George Bernard Shaw to mind, right? You'll probably think of the question raised in "Mrs. Warren's Profession" – the contradictions inherent in capitalist civilization. How enthusiastically did it draw the attention of young people during the May Fourth Movement?

All of Mr. Shaw's works are a critique of capitalist civilization. His style combines humor and cold satire. When we read about the "gentleman soldier" who puts chocolate creams in his bullet box in "Arms and the Man," we will definitely laugh, but in our laughter, we will also definitely feel a thread of bitterness and coldness, right? In this great play, Mr. Shaw exposed all the flattery and embellishment of modern warfare by spokesmen for imperialism! All the big, deceitful lies – what fighting for world civilization, fighting for justice – Mr. Shaw punctures them all with a light laugh!

He is different from Galsworthy, who recently passed away, who also enjoyed great fame in the British theater scene and who won last year's Nobel Prize in Literature. Although Galsworthy's works seem on the surface to also expose the contradictions and corruption of modern capitalist society, at their root he still affirms the current system and defends it.

Since the European War, many old European literary giants who once regarded themselves as warriors of life have reversed course. Those who have not reversed course but are advancing more vigorously towards the light include Romain Rolland in France and George Bernard Shaw in England. Both have denounced the atrocities of imperialism. At a time when the Pacific Ocean is fraught with danger, and imperialism is stepping up its preparations for the division of China and the attack on the Soviet Union in a world war, we welcome George Bernard Shaw's visit to China and hope that he will be able to participate in the survey mission organized by the World Anti-Imperialist League, which will also soon arrive in China!

Ten Greatest People of the Contemporary World 266

— Xue Dakang

I believe that [great men] are not [heroes], and even less are they [powerful officials] or [wealthy people]. Only those who can seek welfare for the [masses], sacrifice for the [masses], or whose words and deeds are sufficient to influence history or even advance history, can be regarded as [great men]. Based on this principle, the [Ten Greatest People of the Modern World] that I have proposed are the following ten:

(1) Gandhi Tagore once said: [Gandhi's life is synonymous with sacrifice.] This is truly a portrayal of Gandhi's entire personality. He led a colonial revolutionary movement in India, and resolutely struggled for the independence and liberation of oppressed peoples. Although his peaceful [non-cooperation movement] has its flaws, the rapid development of India's national independence movement under his leadership is an obvious fact.

(2) Stalin He is the leader of the only [socialist country] in the world today. The success of the Five-Year Plan under his leadership has further consolidated the economic foundation of the Soviet Union, causing capitalist powers to be alarmed and at a loss.

(3) Einstein This is a great scientist. His invention of the [theory of relativity] corrected Newton's [laws of mechanics] and brought about a major revolution in the scientific community. Although he himself once said that there are less than a dozen people in the world who can fully understand his theory, there is no doubt that his work is for the benefit of all mankind. (4) Kemal He is the builder of New Turkey. Under his leadership, the Turkish people, through three years of sustained hard work, defeated the Greek army and saved Turkey from its doom.

(5) Mussolini What is Mussolini? He is a demon and also a maverick. The [Fascist movement] he leads is an obstacle to the progress of the wheels of the times. However, he was able to bring Italy, which was in chaos and weakness after the war, into the ranks of strong countries, and he is ultimately not a [great man.]

(6) Gorky Gorky is the spokesman for the abused masses in the Soviet Union, no, the whole world. He not only speaks out about all the sufferings of the abused masses, but he also encourages, persuades, and guides the literary activities of the [lower classes]. (7) Madame Curie She is the discoverer of radium and has won the Nobel Prize in Physics twice.

(8) Trotsky He personally created the Red Army. In the early days of the Soviet revolution, he commanded twelve fronts. Although he is now exiled for betraying his cause, his great achievements in creating the Soviet Union cannot be denied.

(9) George Bernard Shaw He is a anti-imperialist writer in the most radical imperialist country. He has overflowing talent and rich knowledge. His works are full of humor.

(10) Hoover He is the soon-to-be-out-of-office President of the United States. His plan to suspend war debts and reparations in installments a few years ago gave the world a relatively strong response.

Long Fiction

Crossroads of the Times and Love 267

— Zhang Ziping

[They’re tired, they’ve fallen sound asleep. Damn it!!! Only I’m left here in the middle of the night, unable to sleep! That’s right, that Japanese guy is sleeping in Professor Zeng’s study on the third floor. I didn’t see him go up there tonight. How bold!]

He eavesdropped for a while, but still couldn’t make sense of it, so he returned to the third floor, dejected. He walked to the door of Mr. Zeng’s study again, and gently pushed the door. It seemed to be locked from the inside, so the stone that had been pressing on his chest lightened.

[She must have come to see me, but because I was asleep, she didn’t want to disturb me, so she left.]

He comforted himself in this way and went to bed. He felt that his nerves were a little numb and a little throbbing. He

really wanted to sleep, but no matter what, he just couldn’t fall asleep. He looked at his watch again, it was half past three.

When he woke up the next morning, it was already past seven o'clock. He looked out the window and didn't see any sunlight, just a gray-white sky. He thought, the weather is changing to low pressure again, just like Mrs. Tsuruko's face last night.

In recent days, he had relaxed his schoolwork compared to when he first entered the school, and often skipped classes. So when he got up this morning, he didn't really care whether he would be able to make it to the first class or not. He was just thinking about Mrs. Tsuruko.

[I have already become her prisoner in spirit!]

He had just rolled over and sat up in bed, and was rubbing his eyes. The maid brought him a letter, and he took it in his hand and looked at it. There was no postage stamp on the envelope.

[Who brought it? Not the postman?]

[Not the postman. A young man brought it, dropped the letter, and left.]

He felt that the handwriting on the envelope was familiar, but he couldn't remember who it was from. He hurriedly opened it.

[Brother Haiquan, Mr. Chen invites you to meet him at 8 o'clock tonight. There are matters regarding the literary discussion group that need to be discussed. Please come to my place at half past seven to go together. Knowing this, your brother, the 7th morning.]

Although there was no signature at the end of the letter, he knew that it was written by Tang Yaoxing. After reading the letter, he felt a little unhappy again. First, because the revolutionary writer Mr. Chen Zemin always refused to tell him his address; second, because Tang Yaoxing was always sneaky and never frankly told him their bottom line; third, he refused to sign his real name at the end of this letter. These questions finally aroused Haiquan's antipathy towards them. After reading it, he crumpled the letter into a ball and threw it into the wastebasket. His thoughts turned back to Mrs. Tsuruko. At the same time, he felt an unspeakable annoyance.

He took his toothbrush and towel and walked lazily to the second floor. As he entered the bathroom, he suddenly saw Mrs. Tsuruko's door open. He couldn't restrain himself any longer, and walked forward quietly, wanting to peek inside to see what she was doing in her room.

If he hadn't looked, it would have been better. When he saw the situation in the room, his jealousy exploded.

Mrs. Tsuruko was still wrapped in bed with her hair disheveled, only her snow-white arm was stretched out outside the quilt. She was holding a cigarette between her index and middle fingers, and puffs of white smoke were coming from her mouth. The Japanese guy was still wearing a long Chinese cotton robe, holding a cigarette in his hand, sitting on the edge of the bed at the foot of the bed, leaning against the bed railing, as if he was talking and laughing with Mrs. Tsuruko.

[This is outrageous!]

How to Avoid Tragedy After Marriage? (2) 268

— Gu Fengcheng

Third, the disharmony of each person's thoughts and actions. During courtship, the two sides often rely on momentary impulsive passion or hold the view that [love has no conditions], and rarely pay attention to each other's thoughts and actions. Just look at the love letters, those that focus on the discussion of ideas are a very small minority, most of them are completely the expression of emotions. Sometimes, people may also pay attention to ideological aspects, but their discussions are very superficial and unrealistic, not as practical as discussions with friends. Moreover, during courtship, their thoughts are very easy to converge. For example, if the man is a Christian, the woman, because of her love for him, often becomes a Christian or quasi-Christian. Or if the man was originally a very active youth participating in the revolution, but the woman does not approve of this dangerous and unstable life, then the man often gives up all his work and lives a decadent and hedonistic life with the woman. Therefore, if their thoughts are inconsistent during courtship, two possible tragedies may occur after marriage: the first is that after marriage, it is discovered that each person's thoughts and actions are absolutely or greatly incompatible. The two therefore break up or separate; the second is that after marriage, the man adapts to the woman, or the woman adapts to the man, and as a result, the two go down the road of decadence or indulgence together. As for those who, because of differences in thought and action, can instead go together on the path of a correct and active life after marriage, although there are such people, they are a very small minority.

Fourth, the disharmony of sexual function after marriage is often a major cause of tragedy. We know that sexual desire is one of the human instincts, and sexual life occupies an important part of married life. During courtship, the sexual aspect is often the most neglected. People simply cannot know the other party's sexual situation at all. But after marriage, often all their conditions are suitable, but because the sexual aspects cannot be reconciled, many tragedies occur. Marriage is a union of body and soul. We are not idealists, so of course we cannot rely entirely on the union of souls and ignore sexual harmony. Because sexual desire is a human instinct, the degree of strength of each person is often different; the woman cannot exactly adapt to the man's requirements, and the man cannot exactly adapt to the woman's needs. In this regard, it has a great impact on their future happiness. Also, regarding childbirth, the woman may not want to sacrifice her youth and spirit for the sake of children, while the man very much hopes to have a child. In this regard, they are also incompatible.

Of course, there are other possible causes of tragedy after marriage. I am only listing some of the most common and easily occurring points that are most easily overlooked.

How can we avoid the occurrence of tragedy after marriage? Let's discuss it! (The End)

Talk

Turkish Women's Bathhouse 269

— Bai Xiangci

After the slogan of overthrowing shame and decency was raised, [shame] and [decency] were originally not a problem. Any shameless act could be done boldly, there was originally nothing to say. Although that’s the case, but [a sense of shame and dislike, everyone has it]. When it comes to being embarrassed, one always feels a bit awkward, so I can’t say whether there’s any value in discussing this later on. But we can still talk about it now.

I saw in the newspaper yesterday a funny scene at a Turkish women's bathhouse, which is quite amusing. I will transcribe it below.

In Adana, Turkey, just as a certain women's bathhouse was packed with customers, a female customer shouted wildly [Run for your lives, the building is collapsing!] The order was immediately disrupted. The female customers didn’t have time to put on their clothes. All naked, they ran wildly along the road. As a result, the order on the road was also disrupted by the crowds vying to see the model parade. After investigation, the bathhouse had not collapsed. It was a prank by the female customer, it was said.

Indeed, this funny scene of a model parade must have been quite a sight to see. Many naked women running along the street, shy and embarrassed, must have had a look of embarrassment. If I were in Turkey, I might also be standing by and watching, clapping, laughing, and shouting, [Good show!]

But, no, if I were to meet friends who are accustomed to sunbathing and white female comrades who advocate nude parades, they wouldn’t care about this. They certainly wouldn't change color or lose their composure. They’re accustomed to being naked, so what’s so rare about it? Especially Chinese female comrades, they shouldn’t care, but why is that? I have newspaper evidence.

It was reported in the newspaper last year that a Westerner in Hong Kong initiated a nude convention. Many Chinese and Western women joined enthusiastically, but while Western women nominally joined, few actually did it, while many Chinese women joined and were able to personally try it out. Therefore, the development of the association was largely due to the help of Chinese women.

If we look at it this way, Chinese women are, after all, more open-minded. They can not only talk but also act. I have two more things as evidence. Recently, Western women have been fashionable to go barefoot in the summer, so in the parks at dawn or dusk, one can see many Chinese modern women walking barefoot among them. This shows how strong the imitative nature of Chinese women is. This is one thing. Also, men in various countries mostly cut their hair, while very few women cut their hair, but Chinese women, since recent years, have cut off eighty or ninety percent of their three thousand strands of sorrow, leaving no room for hope. This is another thing.

As the saying goes, [When the city loves a tall bun, those from all directions will raise theirs a foot higher.] Imitating trends and intensifying them is truly a special skill of Chinese women. If Chinese women were to encounter such a trick, I don't think they would blush or turn red. They could just stride onto the road without having to run wildly. The Turkish women's prank wouldn't be worth a smile from an expert.

Science

Photography 270

— Zhidao

Now, if we take a convex lens and place it between a candle flame and a piece of paper, a inverted image of the candle flame will be produced and projected onto the paper. If we insert this lens into a cylindrical tube, so that the inverted image it produces enters a dark box, we have a photographic apparatus. A glass plate is placed at the bottom of the box, coated with a chemical. This chemical changes when exposed to light, which enables the image projected upon it to remain on the glass surface. It photographs an object and captures its image. However, silver chloride is too sensitive to light and is not easily preserved for a long time, so silver iodide or silver bromide are used instead, coated on the glass plate, and placed inside a dark box, to receive light. The ones using silver iodide are wet plates, and the ones using silver bromide are dry plates.

To make a wet plate, first, add a little potassium iodide or ammonium iodide to collodion.

Apply it to the surface of the glass plate to form a thin film (collodion is cotton gunpowder dissolved in alcohol and ether, viscous like glue. When collodion is applied to the glass surface, the ether and alcohol evaporate and the collodion becomes a thin layer.) Next, take the glass plate to a dark room and immerse it in a silver nitrate solution, so that the silver and iodine combine to form silver iodide, which precipitates in the membrane of the glass plate. Place it in a dark box. When taking a picture, the light reflected from the object is stronger than elsewhere, and the silver iodide decomposes, absorbing oxygen and turning into silver oxide. Take it out and immerse it in ferrous sulfate or pyrogallic acid solution. The iodine silver oxide is reduced, resulting in fine silver spots, which are dark black, adhering to the object image. The rest of the sensitized area, because its substance is still silver iodide, is not reduced, thus revealing the object image, called the development. After the image's brightness is suitable, wash it with light, and immerse it in potassium cyanide or sodium thiosulfate solution, then silver iodide dissolves deeply when it encounters it, but the reduced silver does not change and remains, which can make the image more firm, which is called fixing. This image's light and dark are opposite to the real object, but it can be the base of the positive image, and cannot be used for supply, commonly known as the negative. (or called negative image or plate)

To make a dry plate, use gelatin and silver bromide solution, and apply it to the glass plate. Using this plate to take photos, its photosensitive change is faster than silver iodide, so modern people all use this plate, called fast plate. Its development and fixing methods are slightly the same as wet plates.

To get a positive image from the negative, it is advisable to overlay and print with albumen paper once. The albumen is mixed with ammonium chloride, coated on the paper surface, and immersed in silver nitrate solution to form silver chloride. Place it in a dark room to dry it, cover it with a negative, and expose it to sunlight, so that silver chloride is reduced. Turns into silver oxide, showing a purplish brown color, and the positive image of the organism.

The positive is called the printed image, washed, and immersed in a gold plating solution (dissolve a small amount of gold chloride in water and add a little sodium carbonate to make it alkaline), then silver oxide can absorb

the chlorine gas in gold chloride, making gold reduced, and having fine gold spots, being dark purple, adhering to the paper surface, making the object image clear. This is called plating the image.

Blind China National League 271

[The same thing is…] 272

— Cheng Duo

(1) The same thing is that although the weather is cold, and goose feather-like snow is falling non-stop, if you step into the door of a movie theater, you only hear a chorus of voices shouting "Ice cream! Ice cream!" But at the same time, what about the Northeast? The pitiful and loyal volunteer army, they are resisting stubborn enemies and puppet troops in snow several feet deep, with water freezing into ice. They have no support, and soon, when they have no food to eat, they will probably have to eat ice like the people eating ice cream in the movie theater.

(2) The same thing is that in the old Lunar New Year's Eve and New Year's Day, you only hear the sound of firecrackers popping and banging! But at the same time, in the Northeast, the enemy's artillery fire is making the same banging sounds! And what about our loyal volunteer army? Because of the lack of ammunition, they can only make less noise. I wonder why those people who set off firecrackers don't use the money to buy firecrackers to buy ammunition and help the Northeast to make some noise?

(3) The same thing is that in Shanghai, there are many people who smoke opium, and they all have a gun (opium pipe) because that gun is a necessity, without it, they cannot smoke. Now let's talk about the volunteer army in the Northeast. Because they have not received subsidies from the government, their resistance to Japan is entirely out of patriotic thought, so their guns (guns for killing the enemy) are also limited. But without guns, they cannot resist Japan. I think it would be best if all the people in Shanghai who smoke opium abandoned their opium pipes and used the money to buy opium to buy guns for killing the enemy. Wouldn't that be great? But I think it is definitely impossible in reality. (Moving funds to help the Northeast volunteer army)

Profound Performance 273

— Qi Ling

Yuguan has fallen; Old Chen, who considers himself a zealous patriot, bought several extra newspapers and pasted them on the door of the dormitory, writing the five large white characters of "Public Reading Place" beside them in pencil. He also wrote things like "[Fellow students! It's time for us to serve the country!]" and other slogans that didn't quite seem like slogans. Quite a few students were reading the newspapers, so Old Chen was very pleased with himself.

One day, Old Chen saw a passage in the newspaper that read, "Volunteer soldiers engage in hand-to-hand combat with the enemy, flesh and blood flying everywhere..." So Old Chen put on his military uniform, put on the iron helmet he picked up as a Boy Scout during the Shanghai Anti-Japanese War, and dragged Old Zhang, insisting that he accompany him in performing this scene.

"The area outside the pass is snowy and icy; it won't be very realistic to perform it here," Old Zhang hesitated.

"That's fine." Old Zhang came up with an idea. "I'll sacrifice a little." Old Zhang tore up his almost-finished calendar page by page, scattering them upwards, covering the entire room with paper scraps. It immediately looked like a snowy field, and they began to perform.

After a while, Old Chen got bored with the acting. He suggested that they teach Old Zhang to play General Ma Zhanshan, with him playing a Japanese spy, and Old Mao and Old Cheng playing sentries.

The drama began again with profound performance.

Old Zhang sat majestically on the bed, while Old Fan and Old Cheng, with Old Chen's hands tied behind his back, brought him to see Old Zhang.

"Are you a Japanese spy?" Old Zhang said in Mandarin. "You are indeed a spy. General Ma, you are fighting a desperate battle. What madness is this? I think you should surrender to us."

"Bullshit!" Old Zhang, enraged, raised his hand and slapped Old Chen twice, very hard.

"Damn it! We were just playing a role; why did you hit me so hard?" Old Chen revealed his true colors.

"That's what I call a profound performance!" Old Zhang laughed.

Correspondences from Store Clerks

Offering Scholarship | No Fee Required 274

Editor:

Due to our lack of knowledge and other various issues, we feel the need to unite and study together. Therefore, we have gathered several like-minded individuals and formed an "Amateur Academic Research Society." During this process, we have been supported and guided by you, making our society gradually develop. We are truly grateful beyond words! Currently, there are male and female comrades who are interested in academic research—some have volunteered to join, and others have been introduced by existing members—joining our group. So far, there are forty-eight people. However, for the sake of "prudence before organization," the formal establishment of our society still requires considerable preparation.

In the previous preparatory period, we have also held many preparatory meetings, and each meeting has often yielded new proposals, making our organization more perfect. Although there have been minor setbacks, we do not hesitate or become discouraged because of this; we always maintain a spirit of perseverance and strive to move forward.

Recently, we decided on two tasks to be carried out separately: 1) To ensure the legal status of the society, member Zhu Baolin is responsible for handling the registration procedures; 2) Due to the request of most new members, the society's research group will be established in advance. At the last meeting (the 5th), it was decided to temporarily establish four groups: agricultural science, engineering, commercial science, and literature. Furthermore, because many people are willing to study commercial science, the commercial science group has been established, and members Xie Zongyuan and Ni Zi have been elected as the leaders. By the next society meeting—this month's 12th, which is Sunday afternoon at 2:00 PM—research must begin. We not only hope that society members will attend at that time, but also welcome people from all walks of life to our society—located at Xin Zha Road, Da Tong Road, Little Vegetable Market, East Siwen Lane, Xin Zha Elementary School—to listen.

The above is a brief report on the past and present situation of our society. We think: Since you are "happy to support" us, you must also be happy to know. We will continue to report to you on how things progress in the future, but at the same time, we are eager for your guidance and correction.

February 28, 22

××××

Editor's Note: Since this column advocated "organizing groups," many groups have been formed in succession. However, the one that has progressed the fastest and achieved the best results is the "Amateur Academic Research Society." According to the letter, there are already forty-eight male and female comrades who have joined. However, they are not satisfied with this and want to continue their efforts, actually wishing to postpone the establishment meeting. On this point, our opinion is slightly different. Most Chinese people do not have the habit of organizing. To put it bluntly, the comrades of this society are no exception. If one side expands the number of members as much as possible, while the other side cannot effectively organize the group, then in the future, the more people there are, the more complex the opinions will be, and it will be impossible to unite. This is unavoidable. Moreover, if things are delayed in this way, the initial excitement of each member joining the society may be dissipated because of this. We believe that when the number of members reaches more than fifty, the expansion of the number of members should be temporarily stopped, and one or two months should be set aside to focus on discussing and enriching internal issues. After these fifty-odd people have received organizational training and organizational habits, they can then publicly solicit members. At this time, because there are these fifty-odd people as central figures, it does not matter even if some people without organizational habits join. That is our opinion. We wonder if the comrades of this society think it is correct?

As for the two recent resolutions: the first issue of "registration" must of course be handled, but it does not have much value for discussion. The second issue of the "research group" is extremely important, because this is where the spirit of the society lies! The discussion of this issue should focus on two points: "whether the grouping is appropriate" and "whether the method is effective." The opinion on grouping should of course be based on being able to categorize, but the issue of talent must also be considered. In each group, there must be at least one or two people who are somewhat knowledgeable and enthusiastic to take the lead, in order to arouse the strong interest of most members; otherwise, it is better to have quality over quantity. As for the method of research, we hope that the society will send us the records of this research group. We will see if we can find some opinions to offer for your reference.

It is best to allow outsiders to attend the "research group" sessions. Not only can this fully demonstrate your spirit of "helping others," but also, during the period when membership recruitment is suspended, it can create faith in the outside world. When it comes to publicly soliciting members, you can then fully promote it.

Please provide instructions as soon as possible so that I can proceed early. I hereby send this message and await your reply. Respectfully, Guo Aipu. Novel

A Scholarly Family (Continued 16) 276

— Wang Zhongxian

He was very close to several tailors in the alley, because they could tell him stories about jumping insects. He often brought money home to treat them to drinks, pestering them to tell stories, disrupting their work. Sang Aqiang said a few words to him, and he rolled his eyes and scolded:

"This tailor shop was opened by us picking you. This is my place. I am the eldest young master of the family. Who dares to interfere with me? If you continue to act so seriously, I will drive you away tomorrow!"

Sang Aqiang was really angry listening to him, but to reason with him seriously, he was just a child, and he couldn't reason with him. He could only smile dryly at him:

"Good young master, I hope you will be the young master of this house for the rest of your life!"

"What's wrong? Are you angry that I'm being the young master?" Maosheng stuck out his neck, propped his hands on his waist, and swaggered to Sang's boss to provoke him. Sang's boss gently pushed him, and he fell to the ground and cried loudly. The boss's wife, Ali, came out to see what was happening, quickly helped him up, scolded Sang's boss for a while, and coaxed him for a long time, but he still refused to stop. Later, he rushed over and punched Sang's boss in the back dozens of times before he stopped crying and smiled. From then on, Sang's boss called him "Young Master" and dared not offend him again.

After Ruohua came home, Maosheng's arrogance diminished slightly, because this mother did not give him a good face. He did not want to stay at home, and spent the whole day messing around in the tailor shop. The tailors saw that Youzhong came and went very frequently, and deliberately taught Maosheng to go in and spy on Youzhong's movements. Maosheng snuck inside and peeped out, and then told them: sometimes his mother hugged Uncle Wang's face, sometimes they bathed in the same basin, and sometimes they closed the door tightly and couldn't see anything. The tailors also thought it was a fresh topic, and constantly flattered Maosheng, asking him for news, like an outside reporter sticking to someone for news.

One day, Maosheng stole into the inner room to gather news, and took advantage of the opportunity to steal a few cents from the room. Unfortunately, the plan was not airtight, and the maid saw it, grabbed him, and searched for the stolen goods on the spot. The maid reported it to the Madam, and brought him in for questioning. The evidence was conclusive, and he could no longer deny it. Youzhong, who was watching from the side, also advocated that he must be severely punished. So Maosheng was pressed on a bench, and Ruohua personally took action, hitting his buttocks more than a dozen times, making him scream like a slaughtered pig.

Maosheng was punished and went to complain to Ali. He hid the fact that he stole the money, only saying that his stepmother beat him cruelly for no reason and wanted to kill him. Ali had been entrusted by the late Madam to take care of Maosheng and had the power to supervise Maosheng. After listening to Maosheng's one-sided story, she felt that Ruohua was abusing him too much. She took him to see Madam Ruohua.

Home
